        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.6b13421"><meta property="og:title" content="Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS2 Anode"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/acsami.6b13421.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Pyrite FeS2 has attracted extensive interest as anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to its high capacity, low cost, and abundant resource. However, the micron-sized FeS2 usually suffers from poor cyclability, which stems from structure collapse, exfoliation of active materials, and sulfur dissolution. Here, we use a synergistic approach to enhance the sodium storage performance of the micron-sized FeS2 through voltage control (0.5–3 V), binder choice, and graphene coating. The FeS2 electrode with the synergistic approach exhibits high specific capacity (524 mA h g–1), long cycle life (87.8% capacity retention after 800 cycles), and excellent rate capability (323 mA h g–1 at 5 A g–1). The results prove that a synergistic approach can be applied in the micron-sized sulfides to achieve high electrochemical performance."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/acsami.6b13421.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6e81daa56775c-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e81daa56775c-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '946f54f1-09eb-448e-99a4-2f57c1a3e340'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90f6e81daa56775c-SJC"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e81daa56775c-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="90f6e81daa56775c-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Mechanism of Capacity Fade in Sodium Storage and the Strategies of Improvement for FeS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Anode", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.6b13421", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Wan</a></span></span></li><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" data-id="article_author_info" property="author"><a href="/action/doSearch?field1=Contrib&amp;text1=Yunhui++Huang" link"><img height="20" width="27" src="/products/achs/releasedAssets/images/orchid-2856f829046fbda55b90e1582edf0e9a.png" alt="Orcid"></a></span></span></li></ul><div class="affiliations"><div class="article_rightPermissionsLink"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone4" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone4"><div class="articleRightsPermissionsLink"><a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D1536%26pageCount%3D6%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DKongyao%2BChen%252C%2BWuxing%2BZhang%252C%2BLihong%2BXue%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D9%26issueNum%3D2%26contentID%3Dacsami.6b13421%26title%3DMechanism%2Bof%2BCapacity%2BFade%2Bin%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Band%2Bthe%2BStrategies%2Bof%2BImprovement%2Bfor%2BFeS2%2BAnode%26numPages%3D6%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D1541%26publicationDate%3DJanuary%2B2017" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="f_tgr1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/medium/am-2016-13421p_0005.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.6b13421&amp;id=f_tgr1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> has attracted extensive interest as anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to its high capacity, low cost, and abundant resource. However, the micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> usually suffers from poor cyclability, which stems from structure collapse, exfoliation of active materials, and sulfur dissolution. Here, we use a synergistic approach to enhance the sodium storage performance of the micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> through voltage control (0.5–3 V), binder choice, and graphene coating. The FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with the synergistic approach exhibits high specific capacity (524 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>), long cycle life (87.8% capacity retention after 800 cycles), and excellent rate capability (323 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>). The results prove that a synergistic approach can be applied in the micron-sized sulfides to achieve high electrochemical performance.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D1536%26pageCount%3D6%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DKongyao%2BChen%252C%2BWuxing%2BZhang%252C%2BLihong%2BXue%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D9%26issueNum%3D2%26contentID%3Dacsami.6b13421%26title%3DMechanism%2Bof%2BCapacity%2BFade%2Bin%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Band%2Bthe%2BStrategies%2Bof%2BImprovement%2Bfor%2BFeS2%2BAnode%26numPages%3D6%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D1541%26publicationDate%3DJanuary%2B2017" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2016 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291445&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Chemical structure" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Chemical%20structure" class="article__tags__link">Chemical structure</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290640&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Fluoropolymers" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Fluoropolymers" class="article__tags__link">Fluoropolymers</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290677&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Toxicological synergy" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Toxicological%20synergy" class="article__tags__link">Toxicological synergy</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a materials</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Fes2&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_FeS2">FeS<sub>2</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium%20batteries">sodium batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Voltage+Control&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_voltage%20control">voltage control</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Paa-na+Binder&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_PAA-Na%20binder">PAA-Na binder</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Graphene+Coating&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_graphene%20coating">graphene coating</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i1">1 Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Transition metal sulfides have been extensively investigated as energy storage materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 1 to 9">(1-9)</a> Among them, pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> is a very cheap one to be used in Li- or Na-ion batteries. Especially, the primary Li/FeS<sub>2</sub> room temperature batteries and thermal battery have been successfully commercialized. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 10 to 17">(10-17)</a> When applied in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode usually suffers from poor cyclability, which stems from the conversion reaction and drastic structure changes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19 ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19 ref20" aria-label="reference 18 to 20">(18-20)</a> To solve these problems, several strategies have been proposed to improve the cycling stability of FeS<sub>2</sub>. Kovalenko’s group found that the nanosized FeS<sub>2</sub> can exhibit excellent electrochemical performance in sodium storage. When cycling at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the capacity of nanosized FeS<sub>2</sub> can retain 500 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 400 cycles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> Chen et al. proposed that the cycling stability of aggregated FeS<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles can be enhanced via voltage control. When the redox voltage window of FeS<sub>2</sub> is controlled between 0.8–3 V, the cycle life of Na/FeS<sub>2</sub> was improved as long as 20 000 cycles with only the intercalation reaction. However, the application of FeS<sub>2</sub> in SIBs is still inhibited because of the low tap density of nanoparticles and the low capacity (250 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>) that resulted from voltage control. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a></div><div class="NLM_p last">Micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> single crystals are seldom investigated as electrode material in SIBs because of the poor cyclability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14 ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref23" aria-label="reference 14 and 23">(14, 23)</a> However, the active materials with large particle size are desirable in the practical applications to achieve high compacted density, which has been proved in LiCoO<sub>2</sub> in lithium-ion battery. In this work, we prepare the single crystalline FeS<sub>2</sub> micron-particles via a simple solvothermal method. The fading mechanisms of the micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> single crystals were investigated, and a synergistic approach was proposed to achieve high capacity (523.6 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>), high rate (323 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>), and excellent cyclability (87.8% capacity retention after 800 cycles) for the sodium storage.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">2 Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">In this work, graphene was purchased from Nanjing XFNANO Materials Tech Co., Ltd. All the other reagent were purchased from Sinopharm Chemical Regent Co., Ltd., China. All the chemicals were of analytical reagent grade and used as purchased without further treatment.</div><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i3" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i3">2.1 Preparation of Single Crystalline FeS<sub>2</sub> Particles</h3><div class="NLM_p last">FeS<sub>2</sub> particles were prepared by a solvothermal method. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a> First, 1 mmol ferric nitrate (Fe(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>) and 5 mmol thioacetamide (CH<sub>3</sub>CSNH<sub>2</sub>) were dissolved in 35 mL of distilled water, and then 35 mL of monoethanolamine was added to form a dark solution. The solution was stirred for 10 min and then transferred into an 80 mL Teflon-lined autoclave for solvothermal reaction at 200 °C for 48 h. Finally, the product was collected, washed by deionized water, and dried at 60 °C for 10 h in vacuum.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.2 Preparation of Different Kinds of Electrodes</h3><div class="NLM_p">Typically, 70 wt % FeS<sub>2</sub>, 20 wt % super-P (SP), and 10% poly(vinyl difluoride) (PVDF) were mixed in N,N-dimethylformamide (NMP) to form a slurry. The slurry was cast onto a copper foil and dried at 80 °C overnight. Then FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with PVDF binder was achieved (named FeS electrode), and the average mass loading of the electrodes was about 2 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>.</div><div class="NLM_p">The as-prepared FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode was immersed into the graphene solution and taken out immediately, and then the electrode was dried at 60 °C in vacuum. The “dip and dry” step was repeated five times, and then FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with graphene coating was achieved (named FeS<sub>graphene</sub> electrode). The amount of graphene in FeS<sub>2</sub>–graphene composite was determined by measuring the weight of electrode (6 cm × 6 cm slice) before and after graphene coating. The calculated content of graphene in FeS<sub>2</sub>–graphene composite was about 2.86 wt %.</div><div class="NLM_p last">When the PVDF binder was replaced by sodium polyacrylate (PAA-Na) during the preparation process, the FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with PAA-Na binder was labeled as FeS<sub>PAA-Na</sub> electrode.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.3 Characterizations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The crystalline phases of the samples were identified by a X’Pertb PRO (Panalytical B.V., Holland) diffractometer with high-intensity Cu Kα1 irradiation (λ = 1.5406 Å). The morphology was observed by an FEI-Sirion 200 microscope for field-emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM). Transmission electron microscopy (TEM), high-resolution TEM (HRTEM), and energy dispersion X-ray (EDX) spectra were recorded on a JEOL 2100 microscope coupled with an EDX spectrometer (Oxford Instrument). The <i>in situ</i> X-ray absorption data at the Fe <i>K</i>-edge were recorded at room temperature in fluorescence mode using ion chambers or in the fluorescent mode with silicon drift fluorescence detector at beamline BL14W1 of the Shanghai Synchrotron Radiation Facility (SSRF), China. The particle size distribution was measured by a laser particle size analyzer (Mastersizer 3000).</div></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.4 Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The as-prepared FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode was pressed and cut into disks with a diameter of 8 mm. The loading mass of each disk is about 2 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. Then CR2032 coin cell was assembled in Ar-filled glovebox with a counter electrode of sodium foil and a separator of glass fibers. The electrolyte was 1 M sodium trifluomethanesulfonate (NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub>) in diethylene glycol dimethyl ether (DEGDME). The coin cells were galvanostatically discharged/charged at different current densities by Land CT2001 battery testers (Wuhan Land ElectricCo. Ltd., China).</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i7">3 Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The XRD pattern of solvothermally prepared FeS<sub>2</sub> is displayed in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a, showing pure pyrite phase (JCPDS 42–1340). SEM image shows that most of the FeS<sub>2</sub> particles have plate-like morphology. Besides, few nanocubes also exist. According to the laser particle size analysis, the <i>D</i><sub>50</sub> size of FeS<sub>2</sub> particles is about 6.2 μm (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>).</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/medium/am-2016-13421p_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0006.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) XRD pattern of FeS<sub>2</sub> particles; (b) SEM images of FeS<sub>2</sub> particles; (c) cycle performance and (d) charge/discharge profiles of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.6b13421&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">As anode material for SIBs, the micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> delivers an initial capacity as high as 718 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at a current density of 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. The capacity decays slowly during the initial 15 cycles but fades rapidly between 20th and 30th cycles. The capacity only retains 32 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 50 cycles (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c). This demonstrates that the cycle performance is very poor for the bulk FeS<sub>2</sub>. In addition, from the discharge/charge profiles, we can see that the voltage drastically drops with cycling especially after 30 cycles, indicative of an increased polarization (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>d).</div><div class="NLM_p">It has been suggested that the capacity fade of nanosized FeS<sub>2</sub> is closely related with the sodium storage procedure. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> As for the micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub>, <i>ex situ</i> XRD results show that FeS<sub>2</sub> is finally converted into Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S via an intermediate Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>2</sub> phase (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>). This process is consistent with the previous reports by other researchers. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 14 and 23 to 26">(14, 23-26)</a><i>In situ</i> XAFS test was also performed to detect the valence change of Fe during the charge/discharge process (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>). During the discharge process, the Fe K-edge curve moves to the left, which indicates the reduction of Fe<sup>2+</sup> to Fe. During the charge process, the Fe K-edge curve moves to the right, which corresponds to the oxidation of Fe. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14 ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref27" aria-label="reference 14 and 27">(14, 27)</a> However, the profile cannot return to its original position because the charge product is Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>2</sub> instead of pyrite. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22 ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22 ref27" aria-label="reference 22 and 27">(22, 27)</a> From the <i>ex situ</i> TEM, it is observed that the FeS<sub>2</sub> particles tend to pulverize from the outside to inside. After 30 cycles, all the particles are pulverized into nanoparticles (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>). The <i>ex situ</i> EDX shows that after 30 cycles, the S/Fe ratio decreases dramatically from 2 to 0.8 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>). This phenomenon can be ascribed to the sulfur dissolution in the ether-based electrolyte during the conversion reaction. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a></div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/medium/am-2016-13421p_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0007.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Morphology evolution of the FeS<sub>2</sub> micron particles: (a) pristine; (b) discharged to 0.8 V; (c) discharged to 0 V; (d) charged to 3 V; (e) after 20 cycles; (f) after 30 cycles.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.6b13421&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Thus, we summarize the evolution of micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> during sodiation/desodiation in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a. With the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion, pristine pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> is transformed to amorphous Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>2</sub>, and then the Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>2</sub> intermediate phase is further converted to Na<sub>2</sub>S and Fe. When recharged to 3 V, Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>FeS<sub>2</sub> appears again. The conversion reaction in FeS<sub>2</sub> can generate large strain inside the particles, which leads to the structure collapse after 20 cycles. Accordingly, the capacity fade of the micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> can be mainly ascribed to two reasons, that is, particle pulverization and sulfide exfoliation into the ether-based electrolyte.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/medium/am-2016-13421p_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0001.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Schematic illustration of (a) evolution of the FeS<sub>2</sub> micron particles during cycling and (b) strategies to inhibit the fading procedure of micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.6b13421&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">According to the former reports, three strategies have been proposed to inhibit the fading procedure of micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode, as illustrated in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b. First, since the drastic volume change mainly comes from the conversion reaction (0.8–0 V), we can control the redox reaction by tuning the voltage range of intercalation reaction (3–0.8 V). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> As shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a and b, in the voltage range of 0.8–3 V, the micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> exhibits an initial capacity of 380 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> and retains 85.6% capacity after 50 cycles. If the voltage range extends to 0.5–3 V, FeS<sub>2</sub> delivers a higher capacity of 554 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> and only maintains 53.9% capacity after 50 cycles. These results prove that cycling within the voltage range of 0.8–3 V can effectively alleviate the volume change and particle pulverization. However, a narrow discharge depth leads to the low capacity.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/medium/am-2016-13421p_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0002.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Cycling performance of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with different strategies. (a) PVDF binder (0.8–3 V); (b) PVDF binder (0.5–3 V); (c) PAA-Na binder (0–3 V); (d) PVDF binder and graphene coating (0–3 V). The capacities were calculated based on FeS<sub>2</sub>–graphene composite.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.6b13421&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Second, employing proper binder can effectively suppress the exfoliation of active materials. Here, we compare the effects of traditional PVDF and PAA-Na binder. The latter can provide stronger adhesion, more suitable porosity, and hardness. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref30" aria-label="reference 29 and 30">(29, 30)</a> Our experiment shows that the FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with PAA-Na binder delivers a high capacity of 708 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> and a capacity retention of 59.8% after 50 cycles (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>c). This performance is better than that of the electrode with PVDF binder, which indicates that PAA-Na binder can improve the cyclability of FeS<sub>2</sub>.</div><div class="NLM_p">Third, the sulfur dissolution can be suppressed by the interlayer absorption structure. Similar strategy has been widely used in Li–S batteries. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31 ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 31 and 32">(31, 32)</a> Here, we coat a very thin graphene film (&lt;3 wt %) onto the surface of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode. Cycling profile displays that an initial capacity of 690 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> is obtained and the capacity retention is 62% after 50 cycles (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>d). Compared with the bare FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode, the stability of FeS<sub>2</sub> is improved.</div><div class="NLM_p">Obviously, the above strategies all have positive effects on the cycling stability for the micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode, and the improvement mechanisms are further investigated by SEM (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>), TEM (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>), and EIS (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1 and Figure S6</a>). SEM and TEM images show that the FeS<sub>2</sub> particles with PVDF binder are all broken into granules, which indicate a severe structure collapse caused by conversion reaction. Meanwhile, the total charge transfer impedance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) of the electrode increased from 321 to 587 Ohm (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>). However, when the voltage range was controlled in 0.5–3 V, many FeS<sub>2</sub> particles can preserve their original shape, which indicate that incomplete conversion reaction will not destroy all the FeS<sub>2</sub> particles (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>e). Furthermore, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of the cycled electrode is 490 Ohm (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6, Table S1</a>). These results prove that proper voltage control could alleviate the structure collapse and decrease the impedance of the electrode.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/medium/am-2016-13421p_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0003.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. SEM images of pristine FeS<sub>2</sub> electrodes with (a) PVDF binder, (b) PAA-Na binder, and (c) graphene coating; SEM images of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrodes after 30 cycles with (d) PVDF binder cycled in 0–3 V, (e) PVDF binder cycled in 0.5–3 V, (f) PAA-Na binder cycled in 0–3 V, and (g) graphene coating cycled in 0–3 V.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.6b13421&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">When PVDF binder is replaced by PAA-Na, the results show that after 30 cycles, partial FeS<sub>2</sub> particles can retain their original shape, and the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> only increase to 470 Ohm. Therefore, PAA-Na binder could restrain the structure collapse by a stronger adhesive force than PVDF.</div><div class="NLM_p">The graphene-coated electrode is similar to that using PVDF binder, except a graphene layer on the surface. In <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c, an integrated graphene film can be clearly observed. It is worth noting that the impedance decreases largely to 210 Ohm, which proves that graphene coating can efficiently reduce the electrode impedance by better electron transmission. After 30 cycles, it is seen that the graphene film becomes thicker, but most FeS<sub>2</sub> particles can preserve the bulk morphology (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>g). Besides, the ratio of S/Fe is about 1.57, which indicates that the loss of sulfides has been alleviated (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>). Obviously, graphene coating can alleviate the electrolyte corrosion and the structure collapse by physical isolation. What’s more, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> only increases to 249 Ohm, which is much smaller than other electrodes.</div><div class="NLM_p">Depending on above analysis, the electrochemical improvement mechanisms of these strategies can be clarified, that is, proper voltage control will restrain the conversion reaction, and then the structure collapse of the electrode can be alleviated; PAA-Na binder can restrain the structure collapse by a better adhesive force; and graphene coating could not only improve the conductivity of the electrode, but also alleviate the electrolyte corrosion and sulfides exfoliation by the physical isolation effect.</div><div class="NLM_p">However, the above effects are actually limited for the improvement when the strategies are employed separately. Interestingly, if the three strategies are synergistically used, the sodium storage performance of the FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode can be drastically improved. In detail, the FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode was fabricated with PAA-Na binder, and then a thin film of graphene was coated on the surface. During the following sodiation/desodiation process, the voltage range was controlled from 0.5 to 3 V. As shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a, the FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with the synergistic approach delivers an initial capacity of 524 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 200 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and the capacity retention of 87.8% after 800 cycles. Even at a very high current density of 5000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, it can maintain a capacity of 323 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>c). Furthermore, no obvious polarization phenomenon was observed during the cycling (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>b). On the basis of the mass of FeS<sub>2</sub>–graphene composite, the calculated energy densities are about 550 and 350 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> at power densities of 150 and 7500 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, which are superior to the previous works (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>). As above analyzed, running within moderate voltage range (0.5–3 V) can effectively suppress the structure collapse, which gives more stable cycling performance. The PAA-Na binder can further alleviate the exfoliation of active materials from the current collector. Moreover, the graphene coating can mitigate the loss of sulfides and facilitate the electron transmission. Thus, the synergistic approach delivers improved performance over the individual strategy.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/medium/am-2016-13421p_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0004.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. (a) Cycling performance and (b) charge/discharge profiles of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with synergistic approach; (c) rate performance of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with or without synergistic approach.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/asset/images/large/am-2016-13421p_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.6b13421&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i8">4 Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">The fading mechanisms of micron-sized FeS<sub>2</sub> were investigated during the sodiation/desodiation process using <i>ex situ</i> XRD, TEM, and EDX, which stem from the drastic structure collapse, exfoliation of active materials, and sulfur dissolution in ether-based electrolyte. Three strategies were used to improve the cyclability of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode, that is, voltage control (0.5–3 V), PAA-Na binder, and grapheme coating. It is found that the individual strategy provides limited effects on enhancing the cycling stability of FeS<sub>2</sub>, while the synergism of three strategies can exert much more effect. The FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode with the synergistic approach exhibits excellent sodium storage performance by delivering an initial capacity of 524 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 200 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and a capacity retention of 87.8% after 800 cycles. Even at 5000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, it can maintain a capacity of 323 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>. Furthermore, no obvious polarization phenomenon is observed during the cycling. The results prove that a synergistic approach can be applied in the micron-sized sulfides to achieve high electrochemical performance.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.6b13421" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.6b13421</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Particle size distribution of FeS<sub>2</sub> microparticles; <i>ex situ</i> XRD patterns of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrodes in different sodiation/desodiation process; <i>in situ</i> XAFS of FeS<sub>2</sub>; <i>ex situ</i> EDX of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrode during cycling; TEM images of the FeS<sub>2</sub> electrodes after 30 cycles; EIS data and equivalent circuit model of FeS<sub>2</sub> electrodes; energy density and power density contrast of recent work about FeS<sub>2</sub>; <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of different FeS<sub>2</sub> electrodes before and after 30 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b13421/suppl_file/am6b13421_si_001.pdf">am6b13421_si_001.pdf (984.26 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b13421" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin MoS2 Nanosheets as Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Superior Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Dawei; Dou, Shixue; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Few-layer MoS2 nanosheets are successfully synthesized using a simple and scalable ultrasonic exfoliation technique.  The thicknesses of the MoS2 nanosheets ares about 10 nm as measured by SEM (SEM) and at. force microscopy (AFM).  The unique nanosheet architecture renders the high-rate transportation of sodium ions due to the short diffusion paths provided by ultrathin thickness and the large interlayer space within the MoS2 crystal structure (d(002) = 6.38 Å).  When applied as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries, MoS2 nanosheets exhibit a high, reversible sodium storage capacity and excellent cyclability.  The MoS2 nanosheets also demonstrate good electrochem. performance at high current densities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCuMzk1ZvRPbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljP3W9jVLMsfg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVyjtrc%253D&amp;md5=a9d0a91cd4384f49c053101a49ef80c3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b06590"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.                         cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Synthesis of MnS Hollow Microspheres on Reduced Graphene Oxide Sheets as High-Capacity and Long-Life Anodes for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xijun; Ji, Shaomin; Gu, Mingzhe; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Uniform MnS hollow microspheres in situ crystd. on reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanosheets via a facile hydrothermal method.  The MnS/RGO composite material was used as the anode for Na-ion batteries for the first time and exhibited excellent cycling performance, superior specific capacity, and great cycle stability and rate capability for both Li- and Na-ion batteries.  Compared with nonencapsulated pure MnS hollow microspheres, these MnS/RGO nanocomposites demonstrated excellent charge-discharge stability and long cycle life.  Li-ion storage testing revealed that these MnS/RGO nanocomposites deliver high discharge-charge capacities of 640 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 400 cycles and 830 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 after 100 cycles.  The MnS/RGO nanocomposites even retained a specific capacity of 308 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 after 125 cycles as the anode for Na-ion batteries.  The outstanding electrochem. performance of the MnS/RGO composite attributed to the RGO nanosheets greatly improved the electronic cond. and efficiently mitigated the stupendous vol. expansion during the progress of charge and discharge.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqgyxM_04H9CLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljq8W4pYcPH5A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVeqtrbI&amp;md5=76adb4195066af051b440c0c4f12fddd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1039/c2nr31822a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of MoS<sub>2</sub>@CMK-3 Nanocomposite as An Improved Anode Material for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5868</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5871</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered SnS2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composite - A high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life sodium-ion battery anode material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qu, Baihua; Ma, Chuze; Ji, Ge; Xu, Chaohe; Xu, Jing; Meng, Ying Shirley; Wang, Taihong; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

                10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.12.028</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D20%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D168-175%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BCheng%26author%3DN.%2BHan%26author%3DF.%2BZhao%26author%3DP.%2BLi%26author%3DC.%2BJin%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26title%3DTiS2%2BNanoplates%253A%2BA%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BStable%2BElectrode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium%2Bion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2015.12.028&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13421&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2015.12.028&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiS2 nanoplates: A high-rate and stable electrode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yuping; Wang, Hongtao; Cheng, Liang; Han, Na; Zhao, Feipeng; Li, Peirong; Jin, Chuanhong; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">168-175</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Room temp. sodium-ion batteries are of great potential for large-scale energy storage applications because of the abundance and low cost of sodium resources.  However, their future viability will largely hinge on the development of high-capacity and stable electrode materials.  In this study, we report thin TiS2 nanoplates as a possible cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.  These nanoplates possess nanoscale dimensions and large surface areas.  Their interlayer galleries are open toward the edges, providing easy access to the large internal space.  Electrochem. measurements and multiple ex-situ studies demonstrate that TiS2 nanoplates are capable of fast and reversible Na+ intercalation and deintercalation.  They deliver a large capacity close to full Na+ intercalation (186 mAh/g), high rate capability (∼100 mAh/g at 10 C) and satisfactory cycling stability at both low and high current rates.  Our study suggest that with proper nanostructure engineering, two-dimensional layered materials may hold great promise as sodium ion battery electrode materials to enable fast and robust energy storage at low costs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCHwzXUpPW17Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljq8W4pYcPH5A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xlt1Slsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=baef38726f5a7f0a82d344b01d32143a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1021/nn503582c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pang, W.
