K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS<sub>2</sub> to Orthorhombic-SnS</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8323</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8333</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn503582c</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D8323-8333%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DT.%2BZhou%26author%3DW.%2BK.%2BPang%26author%3DC.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DZ.%2BChen%26author%3DH.%2BK.%2BLiu%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DEnhanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BPerformance%2Bby%2BStructural%2BPhase%2BTransition%2Bfrom%2BTwo-Dimensional%2BHexagonal-SnS2%2Bto%2BOrthorhombic-SnS%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnn503582c&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13421&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnn503582c&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS2 to Orthorhombic-SnS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Tengfei; Pang, Wei Kong; Zhang, Chaofeng; Yang, Jianping; Chen, Zhixin; Liu, Hua Kun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8323-8333</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWHE3xEPCjvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgiqbaj289xg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFChtbbJ&amp;md5=4542b1e918e40b9ce5bae292de5dbcf4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b06385"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">An, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sheng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vanadium Sulfide on Reduced Graphene Oxide Layer as a Promising Anode for Sodium Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vanadium Sulfide on Reduced Graphene Oxide Layer as a Promising Anode for Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Ruimin; Wei, Qiulong; Li, Qidong; Luo, Wen; An, Qinyou; Sheng, Jinzhi; Wang, Di; Chen, Wei; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As an alternative system of rechargeable Li-ion batteries, Na-ion batteries revitalize researchers' interest due to the low cost, abundant Na resources, and similar storage mechanism to Li ion batteries.  VS4 has emerged as a promising anode material for SIBs due to low cost and its unique linear chains structure that can offer potential sites for Na storage.  Herein, the authors present the growth of VS4 on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) as SIBs anode for the 1st time.  The VS4/rGO anode exhibits promising performance in SIBs.  It delivers a reversible capacity of 362 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and a good rate performance.  The authors also study the Na storage behavior of the VS4/rGO.  Different than most transition metal sulfides, the VS4/rGO composite experiences a 3-step sepn. mechanism during the sodiation process (VS4 to metallic V and Na2S, then the electrochem. mechanism is akin to Na-S).  The VS4/rGO composite proves to be a promising material for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiEKpa0_88WbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgiqbaj289xg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVeqsb3K&amp;md5=1bd6b7b28b6875016174fb475c0a70f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201504579"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, S.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Ion Storage Properties of FeS-Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite Powder with a Crumpled Structure</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Seung Yeon; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2769-2774</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0947-6539</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion storage properties of FeS-reduced graphene oxide (rGO) and Fe3O4-rGO composite powders with crumpled structures have been studied.  The Fe3O4-rGO composite powder, prepd. by one-pot spray pyrolysis, could be transformed to an FeS-rGO composite powder through a simple sulfidation treatment.  The mean size of the Fe3O4 nanocrystals in the Fe3O4-rGO composite powder was 4.4 nm.  After sulfidation, FeS nanocrystals of size several hundred nanometers were confined within the crumpled structure of the rGO matrix.  The initial discharge capacities of the FeS-rGO and Fe3O4-rGO composite powders were 740 and 442 mA h g-1, and their initial charge capacities were 530 and 165 mA h g-1, resp.  The discharge capacities of the FeS-rGO and Fe3O4-rGO composite powders at the 50th cycle were 547 and 150 mA h g-1, resp.  The FeS-rGO composite powder showed superior sodium-ion storage performance compared to the Fe3O4-rGO composite powder.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqs-8D0ppoyXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgiqbaj289xg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">General synthesis of complex nanotubes by gradient electrospinning and controlled pyrolysis</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Niu Chaojiang; Meng Jiashen; Wang Xuanpeng; Han Chunhua; Yan Mengyu; Zhao Kangning; Xu Xiaoming; Ren Wenhao; Zhang Qingjie; Zhao Dongyuan; Mai Liqiang; Zhao Yunlong; Xu Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanowires and nanotubes have been the focus of considerable efforts in energy storage and solar energy conversion because of their unique properties.  However, owing to the limitations of synthetic methods, most inorganic nanotubes, especially for multi-element oxides and binary-metal oxides, have been rarely fabricated.  Here we design a gradient electrospinning and controlled pyrolysis method to synthesize various controllable 1D nanostructures, including mesoporous nanotubes, pea-like nanotubes and continuous nanowires.  The key point of this method is the gradient distribution of low-/middle-/high-molecular-weight poly(vinyl alcohol) during the electrospinning process.  This simple technique is extended to various inorganic multi-element oxides, binary-metal oxides and single-metal oxides.  Among them, Li3V2(PO4)3, Na0.7Fe0.7Mn0.3O2 and Co3O4 mesoporous nanotubes exhibit ultrastable electrochemical performance when used in lithium-ion batteries, sodium-ion batteries and supercapacitors, respectively.  We believe that a wide range of new materials available from our composition gradient electrospinning and pyrolysis methodology may lead to further developments in research on 1D systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTlCLGWCyeps3ELvajU9pjPfW6udTcc2eZJeYfZgD1Hwbntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2MbjsVKqug%253D%253D&amp;md5=a29f79053b7d3c09ac31b85d243441e8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201401496"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Aken, P.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Encapsulated Pyrite as Stable and Earth-Abundant High Energy Cathode Material for Rechargeable Lithium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Jun; Wen, Yuren; Wang, Yi; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous pyrite nano-octahedra encapsulated by uniform carbon nanocages were prepd. via a facile self-sacrificing template route to serve as an electroactive cathode material.  Due to the shortened Li+ diffusion length, high contact surface area, good electronic cond. and superior structure stability of carbon-encapsulated pyrite, the as-obtained FeS2@C porous nano-octahedra exhibit superior rate capability (a reversible capability of 439, 340 and 256 mA h g-1 at 1, 2.5 and 5C, resp.) and stable cycling performance (approx. 10 % capacity loss after cycles at 0.5C with a capacity retention of 495 mA h g-1).  This work can provide an impetus for further research aiming at utilizing a conversion cathode based on earth abundant FeS2 with the increased energy storage for lithium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpjdNfypa01QLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgiqbaj289xg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFyqur%252FP&amp;md5=9274ea02ad01470c403742b44cfb3d31</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201400934"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ehrlich, S.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Remarkably Improved Electrode Performance of Bulk MnS by Forming a Solid Solution with FeS - Understanding the Li Storage Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Liang; Yu, Xiqian; Yu, Juezhi; Zhou, Yongning; Ehrlich, Steven. N.; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Su, Dong; Li, Hong; Yang, Xiao-Qing; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">24</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5557-5566</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal compds. based on conversion reactions are promising electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries due to their higher lithium storage capacity compared with currently available com. battery electrodes.  Most of the studies on these materials in the literature focus on transition metal oxides and fluorides, and not much work on transition metal sulfides has been reported, partially due to their relatively poor electrochem. performance.  Here, synthesis and characterization of a series of solid soln. FexMn1-xS (x = 0.2, 0.5, 0.8) monosulfide compds. is reported.  Interestingly, hexagonal FeS and cubic MnS can form a solid soln. of FexMn1-xS (x &lt; 0.57).  It is demonstrated that the lithium storage voltage can be tuned by changing the Fe concn. in the FexMn1-xS matrix; meanwhile, the discharge-charge coulombic efficiency and cycle stability of FexMn1-xS are greatly enhanced in comparison with that of pure MnS.  A half cell using Fe0.5Mn0.5S as electrode material achieves a high first cycle coulombic efficiency of 78.0% and a high reversible capacity of ca. 477 mAh g-1 after 35 cycles, while for pure MnS the first cycle coulombic efficiency is only 45.9% and the capacity rapidly fades to ≈200 mAh g-1 after 15 cycles.  Although the solid soln. state of Fe0.5Mn0.5S cannot be retained during conversion reaction as indicated by X-ray diffraction (XRD), X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS), and transmission electron microscopy (TEM), the initial discharge "polarization", which has been considered as one of the major hurdles for conversion reaction, can be significantly reduced by this type of material design.  In addn., the size and distribution of the nucleated nanophases might also be altered by the initial solid soln. state of Fe0.5Mn0.5S, contributing to the improved electrochem. performance reported here.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiVHWVLlo_MLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg0BoFKFWwQ2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFGmurvE&amp;md5=b3700a3e44f0ad44479a5d171242491b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1039/c2jm35227c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">FeS2 synthesized by hydrothermal method was used for Na batteries for the 1st time.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt-Doped FeS2 Nanospheres with Complete Solid Solubility as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Park, Mihui; Zhou, Limin; Lee, Gi-Hyeok; Shin, Jeongyim; Hu, Zhe; Chou, Shu-Lei; Chen, Jun; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering that the high capacity, long-term cycle life, and high-rate capability of anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is a bottleneck currently, a series of Co-doped FeS2 solid solns. with different Co contents were prepd. by a facile solvothermal method, and for the first time their Na-storage properties were investigated. The redox reactions of NaxCo0.5Fe0.5S2 are dominated by pseudocapacitive behavior, leading to fast Na+ insertion/extn. and durable cycle life.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres for superior sodium-iron sulfide batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yun-Xiao; Yang, Jianping; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua Kun; Zhang, Wei-xian; Zhao, Dongyuan; Dou, Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.  The proven conversion reaction between sodium and iron sulfide results in high capacity but severe vol. changes.  Nanostructural design, including of nanosized iron sulfide yolks (∼170 nm) with porous carbon shells (∼30 nm) and extra void space (∼20 nm) in between, has been used to achieve excellent cycling performance without sacrificing capacity.  This sustainable sodium-iron sulfide battery is a promising candidate for stationary energy storage.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical characteristics of Na/FeS2 battery by mechanical alloying</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, T.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To develop the battery with low cost and high energy d., Na/FeS2 battery was prepd. using FeS2 powder synthesized by mech. alloying.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-capacity antimony sulphide nanoparticle-decorated graphene composite as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu Denis Y W; Prikhodchenko Petr V; Mason Chad W; Batabyal Sudip K; Gun Jenny; Sladkevich Sergey; Medvedev Alexander G; Lev Ovadia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes are the main bottlenecks to future developments.  Here we report a uniform coating of antimony sulphide (stibnite) on graphene, fabricated by a solution-based synthesis technique, as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It gives a high capacity of 730 mAh g(-1) at 50 mA g(-1), an excellent rate capability up to 6C and a good cycle performance.  The promising performance is attributed to fast sodium ion diffusion from the small nanoparticles, and good electrical transport from the intimate contact between the active material and graphene, which also provides a template for anchoring the nanoparticles.  We also demonstrate a battery with the stibnite-graphene composite that is free from sodium metal, having energy density up to 80 Wh kg(-1).                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite (FeS2) nanocrystals as inexpensive high-performance lithium-ion cathode and sodium-ion anode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Walter, Marc; Zund, Tanja; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In light of the impeding depletion of fossil fuels and necessity to lower carbon dioxide emissions, economically viable high-performance batteries are urgently needed for numerous applications ranging from elec. cars to stationary large-scale electricity storage.  Due to its low raw material cost, non-toxicity and potentially high charge-storage capacity pyrite (FeS2) is a highly promising material for such next-generation batteries.  In this work we present the electrochem. performance of FeS2 nanocrystals (NCs) as lithium-ion and sodium-ion storage materials.  First, we show that nanoscopic FeS2 is a promising lithium-ion cathode material, delivering a capacity of 715 mA h g-1 and av. energy d. of 1237 Wh kg-1 for 100 cycles, twice higher than for commonly used LiCoO2 cathodes. As sodium-ion anode material, FeS2 NCs provide capacities above 500 mA h g-1 for 400 cycles at a current rate of 1000 mA g-1.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1309-1316</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljRd1Gxax9DQQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b04700"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Douglas, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Carter, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oakes, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Share, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cohn, A.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafine Iron Pyrite (FeS2) Nanocrystals Improve Sodium-Sulfur and Lithium-Sulfur Conversion Reactions for Efficient Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Douglas, Anna; Carter, Rachel; Oakes, Landon; Share, Keith; Cohn, Adam P.; Pint, Cary L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11156-11165</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanocrystals with quantum-confined length scales are often considered impractical for metal-ion battery electrodes due to the dominance of solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer effects on the measured storage properties.  Here we demonstrate that ultrafine sizes (∼4.5 nm, av.) of iron pyrite, or FeS2, nanoparticles are advantageous to sustain reversible conversion reactions in sodium ion and lithium ion batteries.  This is attributed to a nanoparticle size comparable to or smaller than the diffusion length of Fe during cation exchange, yielding thermodynamically reversible nanodomains of converted Fe metal and NaxS or LixS conversion products.  This is compared to bulk-like electrode materials, where kinetic and thermodn. limitations of surface-nucleated conversion products inhibit successive conversion cycles.  Reversible capacities over 500 and 600 mAh/g for sodium and lithium storage are obsd. for ultrafine nanoparticles, with improved cycling and rate capability.  Unlike alloying or intercalation processes, where SEI effects limit the performance of ultrafine nanoparticles, our work highlights the benefit of quantum dot length-scale nanocrystal electrodes for nanoscale metal sulfide compds. that store energy through chem. conversion reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoQ5K7_RKr0B7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljRd1Gxax9DQQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslKlsbbL&amp;md5=04764f41c3057c65e1f434a6b7cca04a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.08.123"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kitajou, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamaguchi, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hara, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Okada, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Discharge/Charge Reaction Mechanism of a Pyrite-Type FeS<sub>2</sub> Cathode for Sodium Secondary Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Discharge/charge reaction mechanism of a pyrite-type FeS2 cathode for sodium secondary batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kitajou, Ayuko; Yamaguchi, Junpei; Hara, Satoshi; Okada, Shigeto</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">247</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">391-395</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The structure changes of FeS2 during discharge/charge process were investigated by x-ray diffraction, XPS and synchrotron-based x-ray adsorption near the edge structure (XANES).  Although the cyclability of the FeS2/Na battery is poor, FeS2/Na battery has a large first discharge capacity of 758 mA-h/g.  It corresponds to 85% of the theor. capacity based on the 4.0 Na reaction per FeS2 (893 mA-h/g).  Based on the Fe K-edge XANES spectra of discharged FeS2 pellets, there were no clear traces of iron valence change.  However, the clear S K-edge jump shifted to lower energy with increasing Na content in FeS2.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium layered oxides with mixed transition metals have received significant attention as pos. electrode candidates for sodium-ion batteries because of their high reversible capacity.  The phase transformations of layered compds. during electrochem. reactions are a pivotal feature for understanding the relationship between layered structures and electrochem. properties.  A combination of in situ diffraction and ex situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy reveals the phase transition mechanism for the ternary transition metal system (Fe-Mn-Co) with P2 stacking.  In situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction using a capillary-based microbattery cell shows a structural change from P2 to O2 in P2-Na0.7Fe0.4Mn0.4Co0.2O2 at the voltage plateau above 4.1 V on desodiation.  The P2 structure is restored upon subsequent sodiation.  The lattice parameter c in the O2 structure decreases significantly, resulting in a volumetric contraction of the lattice toward a fully charged state.  Observations on the redox behavior of each transition metal in P2-Na0.7Fe0.4Mn0.4Co0.2O2 using X-ray absorption spectroscopy indicate that all transition metals are involved in the redn./oxidn. process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVb181OI5yNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lidCtdcCB1LtQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmsFyqsrk%253D&amp;md5=88ccfbeabe627deaf53a8e393488cb77</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1038/nmat2460"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The Li-S batteries have been studied for over 2 decades, as it offers the possibility of high gravimetric capacities and theor. energy densities ranging up to a factor of 5 beyond conventional Li-ion systems.  The feasibility to approach such capacities by creating highly ordered interwoven composites was studied.  The conductive mesoporous C framework constrains S nanofiller growth within its channels and generates essential elec. contact to the insulating S.  The structure provides access to Li+ ingress/egress for reactivity with the S.  It is possible that the kinetic inhibition to diffusion within the framework and the sorption properties of the C aid in trapping the polysulfides formed during redox. The differently neutralized polyacid, alkali and ammonium polyacrylates are examd. as polymeric binders for the prepn. of Si-graphite composite electrodes as neg. electrodes for Li-ion batteries.  The electrode performance of the Si-graphite composite depends on the alkali chems. and neutralization degree.  It is found that 80% NaOH-neutralized polyacrylate binder (a pH value of the resultant aq. soln. is ca. 6.7) is the most efficient binder to enhance the electrochem. lithiation and de-lithiation performance of the Si-graphite composite electrode compared to that of conventional PVdF and the other binders used in this study.  The optimum polyacrylate binder highly improves the dispersion of active material in the composite electrode.  The binder also provides the strong adhesion, suitable porosity, and hardness for the composite electrode with 10% (m/m) binder content, resulting in better electrochem. reversibility.  From these results, the factors of alkali-neutralized polyacrylate binders affecting the electrode performance of Si-graphite composite electrodes are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqXHHurrWVyXrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lidCtdcCB1LtQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjtVGmtg%253D%253D&amp;md5=01696562a51edb46a2a7518cbf6a5a06</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.06.039"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duan, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hong, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xue, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effects of Binders on Electrochemical Performance of Nitrogen-doped Carbon Nanotube Anode in Sodium-Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">174</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">970</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">977</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.06.039</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D174%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D970-977%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DQ.%2BFan%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BDuan%26author%3DK.%2BHong%26author%3DL.%2BXue%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26title%3DEffects%2Bof%2BBinders%2Bon%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BNitrogen-doped%2BCarbon%2BNanotube%2BAnode%2Bin%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2015.06.039&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13421&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2015.06.039&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of binders on electrochemical performance of nitrogen-doped carbon nanotube anode in sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Qingjie; Zhang, Wuxing; Duan, Jian; Hong, Kunlei; Xue, Lihong; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">174</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">970-977</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped hollow C nanotubes (N-CNTs) with turbostratic structure were prepd. as anode materials for Na-ion battery.  The effects of Na polyacrylate (Na-PAA) and poly(vinylidene difluoride) (PVDF) binders on electrochem. performance are comparatively studied.  The obtained N-CNTs have disordered C structure and contain N-, O-functional groups, which electrochem. performance strongly depends on the binder used.  The N-CNTs electrode with Na-PAA binder exhibits large capacity, high initial coulombic efficiency, excellent cycling stability and rate performance.  Compared with the traditional PVDF binder, the water sol. Na-PAA binder shows electrochem. activity, lower internal resistance, and homogeneously formed solid electrolyte interface.  Further the binding capability of Na-PAA is closely related to the mol. wt.  The Na-PAA with moderate mol. wt. is more suitable as the binder of Na-ion batteries with N-CNTs anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqynEBpZSa1S7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lidCtdcCB1LtQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtVWjs7jJ&amp;md5=b9bb5768ffd7c8912d7fb50912e40630</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms2163"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Manthiram, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithium–Sulphur Batteries with a Microporous Carbon Paper as a Bifunctional Interlayer</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Commun.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">3</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1166</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms2163</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D1166%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DY.%2BSu%26author%3DA.%2BManthiram%26title%3DLithium%25E2%2580%2593Sulphur%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2Ba%2BMicroporous%2BCarbon%2BPaper%2Bas%2Ba%2BBifunctional%2BInterlayer%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fncomms2163&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13421&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms2163&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithium-sulphur batteries with a microporous carbon paper as a bifunctional interlayer</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su Yu-Sheng; Manthiram Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1166</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The limitations in the cathode capacity compared with that of the anode have been an impediment to advance the lithium-ion battery technology.  The lithium-sulphur system is appealing in this regard, as sulphur exhibits an order of magnitude higher capacity than the currently used cathodes.  However, low active material utilization and poor cycle life hinder the practicality of lithium-sulphur batteries.  Here we report a simple adjustment to the traditional lithium-sulphur battery configuration to achieve high capacity with a long cycle life and rapid charge rate.  With a bifunctional microporous carbon paper between the cathode and separator, we observe a significant improvement not only in the active material utilization but also in capacity retention, without involving complex synthesis or surface modification.  The insertion of a microporous carbon interlayer decreases the internal charge transfer resistance and localizes the soluble polysulphide species, facilitating a commercially feasible means of fabricating the lithium-sulphur batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTxasvmDUX5qVm8bhe6roZYfW6udTcc2eaFH0M1hKvrX7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3s7hsVCjsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=3a7c59bef3badaff45a11849bf973af3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms9850"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J. T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lou, X. W.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pie-Like Electrode Design for High-Energy Density Lithium–Sulfur Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Commun.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8850</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms9850</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D8850%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BT.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BM.%2BChen%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BW.%2BLou%26title%3DPie-Like%2BElectrode%2BDesign%2Bfor%2BHigh-Energy%2BDensity%2BLithium%25E2%2580%2593Sulfur%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fncomms9850&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13421&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms9850&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pie-like electrode design for high-energy density lithium-sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhen; Zhang, Jin Tao; Chen, Yu Ming; Li, Ju; Lou, Xiong Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8850</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to the overwhelming advantage in energy d., lithium-sulfur (Li-S) battery is a promising next-generation electrochem. energy storage system.  Despite many efforts in pursuing long cycle life, relatively little emphasis has been placed on increasing the areal energy d.  Herein, we have designed and developed a 'pie' structured electrode, which provides an excellent balance between gravimetric and areal energy densities.  Combining lotus root-like multichannel carbon nanofibers 'filling' and amino-functionalized graphene 'crust', the free-standing paper electrode (S mass loading: 3.6 mg cm-2) delivers high specific capacity of 1,314 mAh g-1 (4.7 mAh cm-2) at 0.1 C (0.6 mA cm-2) accompanied with good cycling stability.  Moreover, the areal capacity can be further boosted to more than 8 mAh cm-2 by stacking three layers of paper electrodes with S mass loading of 10.8 mg cm-2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBCkukagMC07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhfPSAJ7gG4Lg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFWlurvK&amp;md5=8bb94632f0158cbed9d4bb2051faa30a</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e81daa56775c-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

The thicknesses of the MoS2 nanosheets ares about 10 nm as measured by SEM (SEM) and at. force microscopy (AFM).  The unique nanosheet architecture renders the high-rate transportation of sodium ions due to the short diffusion paths provided by ultrathin thickness and the large interlayer space within the MoS2 crystal structure (d(002) = 6.38 Å).  When applied as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries, MoS2 nanosheets exhibit a high, reversible sodium storage capacity and excellent cyclability.                         rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiS2 nanoplates: A high-rate and stable electrode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yuping; Wang, Hongtao; Cheng, Liang; Han, Na; Zhao, Feipeng; Li, Peirong; Jin, Chuanhong; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">168-175</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Room temp. sodium-ion batteries are of great potential for large-scale energy storage applications because of the abundance and low cost of sodium resources.  However, their future viability will largely hinge on the development of high-capacity and stable electrode materials.  In this study, we report thin TiS2 nanoplates as a possible cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.  These nanoplates possess nanoscale dimensions and large surface areas.  Their interlayer galleries are open toward the edges, providing easy access to the large internal space.  Electrochem. measurements and multiple ex-situ studies demonstrate that TiS2 nanoplates are capable of fast and reversible Na+ intercalation and deintercalation.  They deliver a large capacity close to full Na+ intercalation (186 mAh/g), high rate capability (∼100 mAh/g at 10 C) and satisfactory cycling stability at both low and high current rates.  Our study suggest that with proper nanostructure engineering, two-dimensional layered materials may hold great promise as sodium ion battery electrode materials to enable fast and robust energy storage at low costs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCHwzXUpPW17Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLjw0npjzWdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xlt1Slsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=baef38726f5a7f0a82d344b01d32143a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1021/nn503582c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pang, W. K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS<sub>2</sub> to Orthorhombic-SnS</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8323</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8333</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn503582c</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS2 to Orthorhombic-SnS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Tengfei; Pang, Wei Kong; Zhang, Chaofeng; Yang, Jianping; Chen, Zhixin; Liu, Hua Kun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8323-8333</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWHE3xEPCjvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLjw0npjzWdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFChtbbJ&amp;md5=4542b1e918e40b9ce5bae292de5dbcf4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b06385"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">An, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sheng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vanadium Sulfide on Reduced Graphene Oxide Layer as a Promising Anode for Sodium Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">As an alternative system of rechargeable Li-ion batteries, Na-ion batteries revitalize researchers' interest due to the low cost, abundant Na resources, and similar storage mechanism to Li ion batteries.  VS4 has emerged as a promising anode material for SIBs due to low cost and its unique linear chains structure that can offer potential sites for Na storage.  Herein, the authors present the growth of VS4 on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) as SIBs anode for the 1st time.  The VS4/rGO anode exhibits promising performance in SIBs. The VS4/rGO composite proves to be a promising material for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiEKpa0_88WbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLjw0npjzWdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVeqsb3K&amp;md5=1bd6b7b28b6875016174fb475c0a70f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201504579"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion storage properties of FeS-reduced graphene oxide (rGO) and Fe3O4-rGO composite powders with crumpled structures have been studied.  The Fe3O4-rGO composite powder, prepd. by one-pot spray pyrolysis, could be transformed to an FeS-rGO composite powder through a simple sulfidation treatment.  The mean size of the Fe3O4 nanocrystals in the Fe3O4-rGO composite powder was 4.4 nm.  After sulfidation, FeS nanocrystals of size several hundred nanometers were confined within the crumpled structure of the rGO matrix.  The initial discharge capacities of the FeS-rGO and Fe3O4-rGO composite powders were 740 and 442 mA h g-1, and their initial charge capacities were 530 and 165 mA h g-1, resp.  The discharge capacities of the FeS-rGO and Fe3O4-rGO composite powders at the 50th cycle were 547 and 150 mA h g-1, resp.  The FeS-rGO composite powder showed superior sodium-ion storage performance compared to the Fe3O4-rGO composite powder.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqs-8D0ppoyXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLjw0npjzWdQ"> &gt;&gt;     </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanowires and nanotubes have been the focus of considerable efforts in energy storage and solar energy conversion because of their unique properties.  However, owing to the limitations of synthetic methods, most inorganic nanotubes, especially for multi-element oxides and binary-metal oxides, have been rarely fabricated.  Here we design a gradient electrospinning and controlled pyrolysis method to synthesize various controllable 1D nanostructures, including mesoporous nanotubes, pea-like nanotubes and continuous nanowires.  The key point of this method is the gradient distribution of low-/middle-/high-molecular-weight poly(vinyl alcohol) during the electrospinning process.  This simple technique is extended to various inorganic multi-element oxides, binary-metal oxides and single-metal oxides.  Among them, Li3V2(PO4)3, Na0.7Fe0.7Mn0.3O2 and Co3O4 mesoporous nanotubes exhibit ultrastable electrochemical performance when used in lithium-ion batteries, sodium-ion batteries and supercapacitors, respectively.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal compds. based on conversion reactions are promising electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries due to their higher lithium storage capacity compared with currently available com. battery electrodes.  Most of the studies on these materials in the literature focus on transition metal oxides and fluorides, and not much work on transition metal sulfides has been reported, partially due to their relatively poor electrochem. performance.  Here, synthesis and characterization of a series of solid soln. FexMn1-xS (x = 0.2, 0.5, 0.8) monosulfide compds. is reported.  Interestingly, hexagonal FeS and cubic MnS can form a solid soln. of FexMn1-xS (x &lt; 0.57).  It is demonstrated that the lithium storage voltage can be tuned by changing the Fe concn. in the FexMn1-xS matrix; meanwhile, the discharge-charge coulombic efficiency and cycle stability of FexMn1-xS are greatly enhanced in comparison with that of pure MnS.  A half cell using Fe0.5Mn0.5S as electrode material achieves a high first cycle coulombic efficiency of 78.0% and a high reversible capacity of ca. 477 mAh g-1 after 35 cycles, while for pure MnS the first cycle coulombic efficiency is only 45.9% and the capacity rapidly fades to ≈200 mAh g-1 after 15 cycles.  Although the solid soln. state of Fe0.5Mn0.5S cannot be retained during conversion reaction as indicated by X-ray diffraction (XRD), X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS), and transmission electron microscopy (TEM), the initial discharge "polarization", which has been considered as one of the major hurdles for conversion reaction, can be significantly reduced by this type of material design.  In addn., the size and distribution of the nucleated nanophases might also be altered by the initial solid soln. state of Fe0.5Mn0.5S, contributing to the improved electrochem. performance reported here.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiVHWVLlo_MLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh20ukCQ9jm4Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFGmurvE&amp;md5=b3700a3e44f0ad44479a5d171242491b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1039/c2jm35227c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes are the main bottlenecks to future developments.  Here we report a uniform coating of antimony sulphide (stibnite) on graphene, fabricated by a solution-based synthesis technique, as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It gives a high capacity of 730 mAh g(-1) at 50 mA g(-1), an excellent rate capability up to 6C and a good cycle performance.  The promising performance is attributed to fast sodium ion diffusion from the small nanoparticles, and good electrical transport from the intimate contact between the active material and graphene, which also provides a template for anchoring the nanoparticles.  We also demonstrate a battery with the stibnite-graphene composite that is free from sodium metal, having energy density up to 80 Wh kg(-1).  The energy density could exceed that of some lithium-ion batteries with further optimization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQGZMXlr7vNCe3MPKNEWB5RfW6udTcc2ea4wJwNlE7HV7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2c3ltFajuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=00d6ac79468675541d9951b7cfb704e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1039/C5NR00398A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Walter, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zund, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kovalenko, M.                         rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite (FeS2) nanocrystals as inexpensive high-performance lithium-ion cathode and sodium-ion anode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Walter, Marc; Zund, Tanja; Kovalenko, Maksym V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In light of the impeding depletion of fossil fuels and necessity to lower carbon dioxide emissions, economically viable high-performance batteries are urgently needed for numerous applications ranging from elec. cars to stationary large-scale electricity storage.  Due to its low raw material cost, non-toxicity and potentially high charge-storage capacity pyrite (FeS2) is a highly promising material for such next-generation batteries.  In this work we present the electrochem. performance of FeS2 nanocrystals (NCs) as lithium-ion and sodium-ion storage materials.  First, we show that nanoscopic FeS2 is a promising lithium-ion cathode material, delivering a capacity of 715 mA h g-1 and av. energy d. of 1237 Wh kg-1 for 100 cycles, twice higher than for commonly used LiCoO2 cathodes.  Then we demonstrate, for the first time, that FeS2 NCs can serve as highly reversible sodium-ion anode material with long cycling life.  As sodium-ion anode material, FeS2 NCs provide capacities above 500 mA h g-1 for 400 cycles at a current rate of 1000 mA g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCSxLuWePxTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b04700"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Douglas, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Carter, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oakes, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Share, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cohn, A.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanocrystals with quantum-confined length scales are often considered impractical for metal-ion battery electrodes due to the dominance of solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer effects on the measured storage properties.  Here we demonstrate that ultrafine sizes (∼4.5 nm, av.) of iron pyrite, or FeS2, nanoparticles are advantageous to sustain reversible conversion reactions in sodium ion and lithium ion batteries.  This is attributed to a nanoparticle size comparable to or smaller than the diffusion length of Fe during cation exchange, yielding thermodynamically reversible nanodomains of converted Fe metal and NaxS or LixS conversion products.  This is compared to bulk-like electrode materials, where kinetic and thermodn. limitations of surface-nucleated conversion products inhibit successive conversion cycles.  Reversible capacities over 500 and 600 mAh/g for sodium and lithium storage are obsd. for ultrafine nanoparticles, with improved cycling and rate capability.  Unlike alloying or intercalation processes, where SEI effects limit the performance of ultrafine nanoparticles, our work highlights the benefit of quantum dot length-scale nanocrystal electrodes for nanoscale metal sulfide compds. that store energy through chem. conversion reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoQ5K7_RKr0B7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCSxLuWePxTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslKlsbbL&amp;md5=04764f41c3057c65e1f434a6b7cca04a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.08.123"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kitajou, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamaguchi, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hara, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Okada, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Discharge/Charge Reaction Mechanism of a Pyrite-Type FeS<sub>2</sub> Cathode for Sodium Secondary Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The structure changes of FeS2 during discharge/charge process were investigated by x-ray diffraction, XPS and synchrotron-based x-ray adsorption near the edge structure (XANES).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium layered oxides with mixed transition metals have received significant attention as pos. electrode candidates for sodium-ion batteries because of their high reversible capacity.  The phase transformations of layered compds. during electrochem. reactions are a pivotal feature for understanding the relationship between layered structures and electrochem. properties.  A combination of in situ diffraction and ex situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy reveals the phase transition mechanism for the ternary transition metal system (Fe-Mn-Co) with P2 stacking.  In situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction using a capillary-based microbattery cell shows a structural change from P2 to O2 in P2-Na0.7Fe0.4Mn0.4Co0.2O2 at the voltage plateau above 4.1 V on desodiation.  The P2 structure is restored upon subsequent sodiation.  The lattice parameter c in the O2 structure decreases significantly, resulting in a volumetric contraction of the lattice toward a fully charged state.  Observations on the redox behavior of each transition metal in P2-Na0.7Fe0.4Mn0.4Co0.2O2 using X-ray absorption spectroscopy indicate that all transition metals are involved in the redn./oxidn. process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVb181OI5yNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLZZ81Ypzu7g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmsFyqsrk%253D&amp;md5=88ccfbeabe627deaf53a8e393488cb77</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1038/nmat2460"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, K.
